  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8e5d8147-5dbc-4081-bf31-e1da11f88c4b'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer1847455512956133947">Dear Reader,<br/><br/>You have undoubtedly picked up this book by mistake, so please put it down. Nobody in their right mind would read this particular book about the lives of Violet, Klaus, and Sunny Baudelaire on purpose, because each dismal moment of their stay in the village of V.F.D. has been faithfully and dreadfully recorded in these pages. I can think of no single reason why</span>
  <span id="freeText1847455512956133947" style="display:none">Dear Reader,<br /><br />You have undoubtedly picked up this book by mistake, so please put it down. Nobody in their right mind would read this particular book about the lives of Violet, Klaus, and Sunny Baudelaire on purpose, because each dismal moment of their stay in the village of V.F.D. has been faithfully and dreadfully recorded in these pages. I can think of no single reason why anyone would want to open a book containing such unpleasant matters as migrating crows, an angry mob, a newspaper headline, the arrest of innocent people, the Deluxe Cell, and some very strange hats. It is my solemn and sacred occupation to research each detail of the Baudelaire children's lives and write them all down, but you may prefer to do some other solemn and sacred thing, such as reading another book instead.<br /><br />With all due respect,<br /><br /><i>Lemony Snicket</i></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1194517-mischenko?shelf=middle-grade-children-s">middle-grade-children-s</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2750176630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13409216032472949810">After finishing up <i>The Ersatz Elevator</i>, we couldn’t wait to start this installment with hopes that the Baudelaires would find a way to locate and save their friends the Quagmire triplets. The book begins with the Baudelaires once again in Mr. Poe’s incompetent hands as he attempts to find them a new and safe home. This time, he’s exhausted all options and finds it extremely difficult locating a place for them. The children are informed that they’ll be living at V.F.D, a.k.a. The Village of Fowl </span>
  <span id="freeText13409216032472949810" style="display:none">After finishing up <i>The Ersatz Elevator</i>, we couldn’t wait to start this installment with hopes that the Baudelaires would find a way to locate and save their friends the Quagmire triplets. The book begins with the Baudelaires once again in Mr. Poe’s incompetent hands as he attempts to find them a new and safe home. This time, he’s exhausted all options and finds it extremely difficult locating a place for them. The children are informed that they’ll be living at V.F.D, a.k.a. The Village of Fowl Devotees, where there are rules for pretty much everything under the sun. This particular town believes in the aphorism, “It takes a village to raise a child” which is the entire basis for taking the children in.<br /><br /><i>One of the women in the Council of Elders spoke up. “We are now discussing the guardianship of the Baudelaire orphans. Under the new government program, the entire town of V.F.D. will act as guardian over these three children because it takes a village to raise a child. Are there any questions?”</i><br /><br />What the Baudelaires don’t know yet, is that the town of V.F.D. is incredibly disturbing and full of crows, but they still have hope that the Quagmire triplets are there. Unfortunately, the children have been put in the hands of an entire village of idiots and all they can do is search for clues to find their friends once and for all.<br /><br /><i>“Now, Baudelaires, I’m sure you are very concerned about this Olaf fellow, but as your guardian, the town will protect you. That is why we have recently made up a new rule, Rule #19,833. It clearly states that no villains are allowed within the city limits.”</i><br /><br />This book was quite slow for the first half, but then we ended up flying through the second half because it’s fairly action packed. The story itself wasn’t as comical, but there are additional characters which was nice. There's also an interesting mystery to it and it's fairly unpredictable.<br /><br />Even though the series is quite formulaic, the kids always end up enjoying these. The author manages to instill hope in the reader with every book, but unfortunately, something always goes wrong and Count Olaf prevails. This book is a little darker, ends a little bit differently, and we have no idea what predicament the children will be in next with the way this one ended.<br /><br />4****<br /><br />You can also read this @ <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.readrantrockandroll.com">www.readrantrockandroll.com</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3651102138916338964">I am legally obligated to begin every review of my reread of these books with the following sentiment: I LOVE THIS SERIES SO MUCH.<br/><br/>It is a legal obligation of my own construction, because I do love these books and cherish them with everything I have in my cold dead heart, but also…<br/><br/>Also this wasn’t my FAVORITE of the series.   <span id="freeText3651102138916338964" style="display:none">I am legally obligated to begin every review of my reread of these books with the following sentiment: I LOVE THIS SERIES SO MUCH.<br /><br />It is a legal obligation of my own construction, because I do love these books and cherish them with everything I have in my cold dead heart, but also…<br /><br />Also this wasn’t my FAVORITE of the series. Which really, if you think about it? A book in my favorite series that isn’t necessarily my favorite of the series - still pretty good. Not the end of the world or anything.<br /><br />Maybe the fact that I was slumping so hard that even a children’s book in a world I adore took me 5 days to read has something to do with it.<br /><br />Or - or, or, or - maybe this book just feels kind of sloppier than the others. WHICH DON’T GET ME WRONG - even sloppy Lemony Snicket is more precise than literally anyone writing YA fantasy in the last hundred thousand years. (You know. Because the genre of YA fantasy has definitely been around since the beginning of time.)<br /><br />Maybe both.<br /><br />Or maybe I just love to complain even when it comes to my FAVORITE SERIES OF ALL TIME.<br /><br />Bottom line: I hate myself.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1107821590" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1107821590" />
    <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence"><img alt="Mark Lawrence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442536170p2/4508542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1107821590?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark Lawrence" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence">Mark Lawrence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1107821590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14912494896654534840">The Vile Village is where the whole VFD thing really starts to take off and the original formula of a new guardian followed by Olaaf turning up in a new disguise starts fraying.<br/><br/>The village is quite fun, replete with dozens of vile villagers, hundreds of ridiculous rules, and thousands upon thousands of crows.<br/><br/>The off-beat humour continues with Sunny's one worders and their elaborate translation, and the extreme stupidity of everyone who isn't a Baudelaire.<br/><br/>The penalty for breaking almost any villa</span>
  <span id="freeText14912494896654534840" style="display:none">The Vile Village is where the whole VFD thing really starts to take off and the original formula of a new guardian followed by Olaaf turning up in a new disguise starts fraying.<br /><br />The village is quite fun, replete with dozens of vile villagers, hundreds of ridiculous rules, and thousands upon thousands of crows.<br /><br />The off-beat humour continues with Sunny's one worders and their elaborate translation, and the extreme stupidity of everyone who isn't a Baudelaire.<br /><br />The penalty for breaking almost any village law is to be burned at the stake - which seems pretty gruesome in a children's story. And we come pretty close to seeing it carried out.<br /><br />Perhaps though this story is most memorable for the WORST INVENTION EVER. Violet's inventing skills are put to the test when the children need to break out of a jail cell. The solution is to pour water from a jug ... along a bench ... and onto the wall where it ... weakens the mortar between the bricks. The water is then mopped up with bread, the bread is squeezed over the jug, the process is repeated. ... and it works.<br /><br />The Quagmires are back again. The Baudelaires hunt for them in a book-spanning plot that makes no sense at all, involving clues sent by the Quagmires. And they're eventually found in a location ... that, at the risk of repeating myself, MAKES NO SENSE AT ALL. <br /><br />In fact, very little of this book makes any sense. But, Celyn enjoyed me reading it to her, and it's an OK book, little better or worse than its mid-series predecessors. <br /><br /><br /> <a href="http://eepurl.com/cimnK1" rel="nofollow noopener">Join my 3-emails-a-year newsletter #prizes</a><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />….</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText4030955387858063928" style="display:none">Here at the halfway point of the series, the author is finally dropping more hints and clues about what seems to be a rather large conspiracy against the Baudelaire orphans, the Quagmire orphans, and I gather orphans everywhere who have large fortunes to be acquired. <br /><br />The search for the Quagmire triplets in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/131122.The_Ersatz_Elevator__A_Series_of_Unfortunate_Events___6_" title="The Ersatz Elevator (A Series of Unfortunate Events, #6) by Lemony Snicket" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ersatz Elevator</a> ended with a literal red herring, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/335131.The_Vile_Village__A_Series_of_Unfortunate_Events___7_" title="The Vile Village (A Series of Unfortunate Events, #7) by Lemony Snicket" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vile Village</a> is almost entirely red herring, as the children are sent to become the wards of a village known only by the mysterious letters "V.F.D." Having chased the meaning of these letters since the end of the fifth book, the orphans believe they're close to an answer. <br /><br />Though answers are not necessarily forthcoming, the new clues continue to be tantalizing, a word which here means "something that increases your enjoyment of the series in spite of the figurative red herrings."<br /><br />EDIT: I'm somewhat surprised that this little review has so many 'likes.' I have so many better reviews! </span>

  <span id="freeText12039011001367254573" style="display:none">The Vile Village (Unfortunate Events #7), Lemony Snicket<br />The Vile Village is the seventh novel in the children's book series A Series of Unfortunate Events by Lemony Snicket (the pen name of American author Daniel Handler), which consists of 13 children's novels that follow the turbulent lives of Violet, Klaus, and Sunny Baudelaire after their parents' death. The children are placed in the custody of their distant cousin/uncle Count Olaf, who attempts to steal their inheritance.   <span id="freeText6766254352886241334" style="display:none"><i>For Beatrice – When we were together I felt breathless. Now you are.</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565695649ra/27985517.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For their seventh misadventure, the Baudelaire orphans are sent to a creepy village, completely covered with crows, and full of impossible, vile rules against inventing, reading, and biting! How are they ever going to escape yet another, inevitable, encounter with the horrible count Olaf if they can't put their best abilities to use? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1565695755ra/27985524.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I enjoyed this adventure so much! It was ok, there were some cute parts. I like that the book always has some spot-on satire about society and adults especially. This book did push the series along a bit but I'm getting tired of the formula with these books. Orphans go to terrible place, all the adults are horrible human beings, the orphans are forced to do insane things for the adults, one adult is always nice but useless and in the end they escape but just barely. I did think this one had a couple of moments that were a bit darker, which I always appreciate but overall I pushed to get through it. It's a very fast read though. I read it in like an hour or two. <br /><br />I would still recommend it because the series is fun and if you have a child then this would probably be a hit. </span>

As the series goes on, the books really become more intricate and mature and I find that's particularly prominent in this one! </span>

<div id="review_150545299" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/150545299" />
    <a title="Nicholas Karpuk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1574263-nicholas-karpuk"><img alt="Nicholas Karpuk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442509877p2/1574263.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/150545299?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicholas Karpuk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicholas Karpuk" href="/user/show/1574263-nicholas-karpuk">Nicholas Karpuk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150545299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13189908321556907982">If I had to draw a line in the sand with the Snicket books between overly formulaic but funny, and genuinely well put together, I'd put it within the first few chapters of The Vile Village.<br/><br/>There's a few things absent from this read through, most of them positive. He isn't constantly reiterating the three children's skills in a "this is for Violet, this is for Klaus, this is for Sunny" sort of rhythm. There guardian is slightly more relatable, and altogether decent guy who gets severely skittish </span>
  <span id="freeText13189908321556907982" style="display:none">If I had to draw a line in the sand with the Snicket books between overly formulaic but funny, and genuinely well put together, I'd put it within the first few chapters of The Vile Village.<br /><br />There's a few things absent from this read through, most of them positive. He isn't constantly reiterating the three children's skills in a "this is for Violet, this is for Klaus, this is for Sunny" sort of rhythm. There guardian is slightly more relatable, and altogether decent guy who gets severely skittish around authority. And they actually get some answers to the larger mysteries along with a growing integration of Lemony Snicket as a character rather than a pure narrator.<br /><br />Plus it just flat out reads better. The structure is looser, giving more room for whimsical turns of events.<br /><br />If there's an over-arching theme to the Unfortunate Events, it's the perils of adulthood. Every book discusses the dismissiveness of adults towards children, but each covers more specific territory. In this case, it's legalism, as the town they're adopted by is run by old people obsessed with maintaining a seemingly self-contradicting body of laws.<br /><br />Snicket works in defiance of the Nickelodeon model of pro-kid entertainment, where kids are constantly triumphing over adults. Most savvy kids get irritated with this after a while, as they spend most of their childhood getting regularly thwarted by adults. Power fantasies only hold the attention of some people for a short time.<br /><br />Instead he treats childhood as a kind of tragedy, where foolhardy adults with their various issues often railroad kids into terrible lives. What's secretly positive about this very bleak series is that the only way the children outwit adults is through positive traits like self-reliance, critical analysis, and research. Klaus actually reads the entire rulebook for the town, something none of the elders actually appear to have done. <br /><br />The Vile Village in particular shows that to outwit the elderly tyrants in your life, you have to be smarter, more clever, and braver. What's impressive is that it makes it sound perfectly achievable.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13189908321556907982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2683045881" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer17461421664615787548"><b>3.2/5</b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>"For sapphires we are held in here.<br/>Only you can end our fear."</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>This is definitely my <b>least favorite</b> out of the whole series so far.<br/>It was just okay, nothing exciting happens in here.<br/><br/><b>I liked at the beginning the idea of the entire village</b> that adopts the kids and all the absurd rules that were created for the habitants.<br/><b>Then it became pretty boring</b> to be honest. <b>The most exciting part was definitely the "riddles"</b> that were left for the children by their missing friends.<br/>It was fun to build </span>
  <span id="freeText17461421664615787548" style="display:none"><b>3.2/5</b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"For sapphires we are held in here.<br />Only you can end our fear."</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />This is definitely my <b>least favorite</b> out of the whole series so far.<br />It was just okay, nothing exciting happens in here.<br /><br /><b>I liked at the beginning the idea of the entire village</b> that adopts the kids and all the absurd rules that were created for the habitants.<br /><b>Then it became pretty boring</b> to be honest. <b>The most exciting part was definitely the "riddles"</b> that were left for the children by their missing friends.<br />It was fun to build the whole poem slowly and find out what really meant in the end. <br /><br />Another flaw is that <b>there's basically no Count Olaf here</b>, so maybe that's a fact that made this book way less exciting. <br />He's no messing with the kids that much, there's almost no disguise and interaction with them.<br />After the previous book that I loved <b>this was pretty disappointing.</b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2303734087204419507">2.5 stars <br/><br/>Seventh book already and the plot of this one doesn't really differ much from its predecessors. And I'm getting a bit tired of it... And I am so frustrated about the adult's logic in this world! The same thing happens over and over, yet no one believes the Baudeliere children. <br/><br/>I feel like the readers haven't been given answers to the bigger mysteries of this series. Although, Lemony Snicket is slowly dropping hints and facts of a bigger overall series storyline here, sometimes, I still</span>
  <span id="freeText2303734087204419507" style="display:none">2.5 stars <br /><br />Seventh book already and the plot of this one doesn't really differ much from its predecessors. And I'm getting a bit tired of it... And I am so frustrated about the adult's logic in this world! The same thing happens over and over, yet no one believes the Baudeliere children. <br /><br />I feel like the readers haven't been given answers to the bigger mysteries of this series. Although, Lemony Snicket is slowly dropping hints and facts of a bigger overall series storyline here, sometimes, I still can't help but feel like it's kind of a drag. I'm hoping the next books would somehow pick up from there and have some diversity.<br /><br />Maybe if I was still a teenager, I'd enjoy it more.<br /><br />The only reason I wanna finish this series now is because I'm excited for the upcoming TV series.</span>

<div id="review_86004815" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/86004815" />
    <a title="Casey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2566703-casey"><img alt="Casey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466532567p2/2566703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/86004815?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Casey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Casey" href="/user/show/2566703-casey">Casey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780064408653" href="/book/show/335131.The_Vile_Village">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer86004815&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer86004815" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer277015741471906425">Finally, finally, finally! I loved this one. I've gone beyond simply admiring the wit of the author and am seeing the makings of a great fictional world in this tale.<br/><br/>First of all, with Hector, we have the first character over the age of 14 who functions at a basic human level and is not a criminal mastermind. He listens with an open mind, takes notice of others outside of himself, and EVOLVES AS THE STORY PROGRESSES. He goes from a kindly (albeit cowardly) man to something of a hero when he fina</span>
  <span id="freeText277015741471906425" style="display:none">Finally, finally, finally! I loved this one. I've gone beyond simply admiring the wit of the author and am seeing the makings of a great fictional world in this tale.<br /><br />First of all, with Hector, we have the first character over the age of 14 who functions at a basic human level and is not a criminal mastermind. He listens with an open mind, takes notice of others outside of himself, and EVOLVES AS THE STORY PROGRESSES. He goes from a kindly (albeit cowardly) man to something of a hero when he finally learns to speak up for himself and others in order to do the right thing. That is what has been missing from the caricatures that pass for adults in this series.<br /><br />I found myself worrying about the safety of the Quagmire children, and biting my nails when I thought the six of them wouldn't get away on the balloon in the end. This is because this time, the story introduced me to characters to whom I could relate, and about whom I could care.<br /><br />Even more importantly, the conspiracy and continuity of the storyline has finally taken center stage. We are now less concerned with isolated incidents that happen to the orphans and more focused on consolidating and analyzing little hints from all of the books to solve the overarching puzzle. It sharpens the readers' skills and heightens their interest.<br /><br />This, to me, is what makes a truly "good read."</span>
  <a data-text-id="277015741471906425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2112298834" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2112298834" />
    <a title="Alaina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50620706-alaina"><img alt="Alaina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451325817p2/50620706.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2112298834?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alaina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alaina" href="/user/show/50620706-alaina">Alaina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=january-2019">january-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2112298834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10012446806250919433">Uhh... interesting?<br/><br/><i>The Vile Village</i> is the seventh installment of the <i>A Series of Unfortunate Events</i> series. It was a really one that kind of threw me for a loop. My freaking favorite character, Sunny, was definitely the reason why. <br/><br/>Okay so this village is, again, weird. The people and basically everything about it is weird. I pretty much blame this whole weird creepy village for the kids acting stranger than they usually are. For instance, Sunny was just ugh in it. I mean, she eventually came a</span>
  <span id="freeText10012446806250919433" style="display:none">Uhh... interesting?<br /><br /><i>The Vile Village</i> is the seventh installment of the <i>A Series of Unfortunate Events</i> series. It was a really one that kind of threw me for a loop. My freaking favorite character, Sunny, was definitely the reason why. <br /><br />Okay so this village is, again, weird. The people and basically everything about it is weird. I pretty much blame this whole weird creepy village for the kids acting stranger than they usually are. For instance, Sunny was just ugh in it. I mean, she eventually came around to something likable.. but still, why the change? Then there's the whole sibling fighting thing - which is very common, but it broke my heart a little bit. <br /><br />Other than that, Olaf is definitely stepping up his game. I had thought so many people were actually him in disguise.. to find out that I was completely wrong. It was very intriguing and kept me highly entertained with this book. I kind of wish these books were a bit longer because I fly through them. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10012446806250919433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_277191'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/277191.The_Ironwood_Tree"><img alt="The Ironwood Tree (The Spiderwick Chronicles, #4)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1417954144l/277191._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KNnl5tpavTGA3CUizW2Vq96qttQJF1r01s5yG5CJ8zqGRWjGUKIHwUdicv6OkzF6ZbzTTS7vvM0n/fHmOCKa2A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }
